## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The equation of motion typically involves restoring forces (functions of x) and damping terms (functions of v), possibly with nonlinear contributions like cubic terms (Duffing oscillator) or nonlinear damping (van der Pol oscillator).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-varying stiffness)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force → negative proportionality to displacement: c0 * x with c0 < 0
- Nonlinear stiffness (hardening/softening) → odd-power terms in position: x**3, x**5
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → cubic position term (Duffing-type x**3)
- Self-sustained oscillation → velocity-dependent terms with sign change: (1 - x**2)*v (van der Pol type)
- Energy dissipation → odd-power velocity terms: v, v**3 with negative coefficients
- Symmetry breaking → even-power position terms: x**2 introduces asymmetry in the potential
- Position-velocity coupling → product terms x*v or x**2*v indicate nonlinear damping dependent on amplitude
- Periodic forcing → sinusoidal time dependence: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) as additive terms

**GT:** `-0.0493727*v³ - 1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- The x terms: `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x = -1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x = -0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`
- So GT = `-2.05860*x - 0.02293*t*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.04937*v³ - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `t*x`
3. `sin(t)`
4. `v³`
5. `|v|^(1/3)`

There's no constant offset term (though candidates with `c1` constant could set it to 0).

The critical term is `|v|^(1/3)` — this is `Abs(v)^(1/3)`, which is NOT the same as `v^(1/3)` since v can be negative.

Let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1 + c2*sin(t) + c3*v**c4 + c5*t*x + c6*v*x² + c7*v³`
Has `v**c4` which could be `v^(1/3)`, but GT needs `|v|^(1/3)`. Since v takes both signs, `v^(1/3)` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)`. Also has extra `v*x²` term (set c6=0). But the `|v|^(1/3)` issue remains.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `c0*x + c1 + c2*sin(t) + c3*v**c4 + c5*t*x + c6*v³`
